<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8825353402245548507">Someone is after Beryl Madison -- spying on her, making threatening phone calls. Terrified, she flees to Key West. When she comes back home it's not harassment that's waiting...it's murder. Someone kills her, someone she trusted enough to open her door to.<br /><br />Police work begins with Dr. Kay Scarpetta, Chief Medical Examiner. She finds laboratory clues no one wants to believe.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8825353402245548507">Someone is after Beryl Madison -- spying on her, making threatening phone calls. Terrified, she flees to Key West. When she comes back home it's not harassment that's waiting...it's murder. Someone kills her, someone she trusted enough to open her door to.<br /><br />Police work begins with Dr. Kay Scarpetta, Chief Medical Examiner. She finds laboratory clues no one wants to believe. So she follows them herself, putting her professional career -- and her life -- on the line.<br /><br />"Cornwell makes looking through a microscope as exciting as hot pursuit." (Washington Post)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_411377912">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411377912" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11895609-faye" class="left imgcol" title="Faye"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448813101p2/11895609.jpg" alt="Faye" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/411377912?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 02, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11895609-faye" class="user" title="Faye">Faye</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7533147-body-of-evidence" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11895609-faye?shelf=crime-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11895609-faye?shelf=re-read-in-2015" class="actionLinkLite">re-read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11895609-faye?shelf=1990-1999" class="actionLinkLite">1990-1999</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11895609-faye?shelf=four-stars" class="actionLinkLite">four-stars</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11895609-faye?shelf=kay-scarpetta-series" class="actionLinkLite">kay-scarpetta-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer411377912">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4225848296382044847">First read: c. 2005<br />Re-read: August 2015<br />Plot: Scarpetta and Marino must track down the stalker/ killer of a talented young writer, while at the same time a romantic interest from Kay's past makes an appearance and seems more involved in the case Kay is investigating than it first appears.<br /><br />What I liked:<br /><br />- Opening of the novel with the letters written by Beryl, they are lovely and descriptive.<br /><br />- The literary themed mystery. I thought some of the scenes seemed to be an homage to Agatha Christie's myste</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4225848296382044847">First read: c. 2005<br />Re-read: August 2015<br />Plot: Scarpetta and Marino must track down the stalker/ killer of a talented young writer, while at the same time a romantic interest from Kay's past makes an appearance and seems more involved in the case Kay is investigating than it first appears.<br /><br />What I liked:<br /><br />- Opening of the novel with the letters written by Beryl, they are lovely and descriptive.<br /><br />- The literary themed mystery. I thought some of the scenes seemed to be an homage to Agatha Christie's mysteries <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ for example the death of Sterling Harper which took place almost right under Kay's nose  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and the island scene where Kay investigates on her own. <br />I also thought Cary Harper- the Pulitzer prize winning novelist who only wrote one book which was about racism in the deep south - was a clear (although male) parody of Harper Lee, which is something I didn't pick up on ten years ago when I first read the book. Considering some of the scandals surrounding the fictitious Cary Harper I wonder why Cornwell chose to base the character on Harper Lee? It makes me want to read more about Harper Lee's life to see if the similarities between them are more than just superficial.<br /><br />- I like that Kay was more friendly to Marino in this book and acknowledges everything he did for her at the end of Postmortem.<br /><br />What I disliked:<br /><br />- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ I don't understand why each book has to end with the killer becoming obsessed with Kay and trying to kill her in the same way he murdered his previous victims. It happened in Postmortem and again in Body of Evidence. I would think Kay would be traumatised as a result of all the attempted murders against her!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ Mark betrayed Kay's trust, set her up in a confrontation with a man who tried to ruin her professionally and she still sleeps with him at the end of the novel. The novel ends with the hint that Mark might become a permanent love interest in the series, but as this is a re-read for me, I know better :)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />- Lucy doesn't appear in this instalment, and there are only a few cameos by Benton :(<br /><br />Overall rating: 4/5 stars.<br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4225848296382044847">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/42364341?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 08, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1328950-judy" class="user" title="Judy">Judy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/1328950-judy?shelf=female-author" class="actionLinkLite">female-author</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer42364341">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16786006941153202683">This series is what I call a "guilty pleasure". Not at all high-brow, but easy to read thrillers with some mystery, and I have to admit that I enjoy the gruesome details about forensic pathology. Being an engineering type, I like to know the details behind things, how things work, in particular when it comes to problem solving or investigative techniques.<br /><br />I do love the character of Kay Scarpetta; she's a strong, smart woman who is also attractive. She makes me nuts sometimes when she does risky t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16786006941153202683">This series is what I call a "guilty pleasure". Not at all high-brow, but easy to read thrillers with some mystery, and I have to admit that I enjoy the gruesome details about forensic pathology. Being an engineering type, I like to know the details behind things, how things work, in particular when it comes to problem solving or investigative techniques.<br /><br />I do love the character of Kay Scarpetta; she's a strong, smart woman who is also attractive. She makes me nuts sometimes when she does risky things that her superior brain should be telling her not to do, but then there wouldn't be a story, would there?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16786006941153202683">...more</a>

              <a href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=crime-thriller-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">crime-thriller-suspense</a>,

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer768391785">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10114107926145055732">3.5 stars. Not nearly as good as the first in the series, but I know this series gets better. I don't think I ever read this one, though. There were some interesting twists in this, definitely not what I would have guessed. A solid entry in the series, but without the crackle of the first, <a title="Postmortem (Kay Scarpetta, #1) by Patricia Cornwell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6534.Postmortem__Kay_Scarpetta___1_">Postmortem</a>. I'll definitely continue with the series. </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer19657394">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6744110035417644425">I used to teach this installment of the Scarpetta series as the example of the "mystery" genre in a novels class.<br /><br />Basic Plot: a writer of historical romances is found murdered, and Kay Scarpetta is on the case again.<br /><br />Considering the fact that I taught this book, I remember it fairly well, even years after reading it. The pacing was good and there were plenty of red herrings that I used to love to use to torture my students with. If I have any complaints about it, they lie in the fact that the "big</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6744110035417644425">I used to teach this installment of the Scarpetta series as the example of the "mystery" genre in a novels class.<br /><br />Basic Plot: a writer of historical romances is found murdered, and Kay Scarpetta is on the case again.<br /><br />Considering the fact that I taught this book, I remember it fairly well, even years after reading it. The pacing was good and there were plenty of red herrings that I used to love to use to torture my students with. If I have any complaints about it, they lie in the fact that the "big reveal" completely comes out of left field. I like to read clues through a story and figure things out with (before if possible) the main character, and this book didn't allow for that. This is dangerously close to a spoiler, so I'm stopping the description there.<br /><br />I like Kay as a character: logical, older, and a bit pudgy. She's relatable to me and not a "perfect" person. This 2nd book in the series allows the character to grow a bit from the first volume and readers also get to see more of her back story.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/481864821?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 07, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5903843-matt" class="user" title="Matt">Matt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/132336.Body_of_Evidence" title="Paperback 9780743493918" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer481864821">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14823287667408695686">Cornwell brings Dr. Kay Scarpetta back in the critically acclaimed series to test her wiles in a new and disturbing manner. When a murdered author is found in her home, investigators are left with little to know insight, which bothers Scarpetta almost as much as the slaying itself. Questions grow exponentially while answers remain deftly hidden behind layers of the victim’s past. Scarpetta and the police being piecing things together, discovering a deeper back story related to her current piece</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14823287667408695686">Cornwell brings Dr. Kay Scarpetta back in the critically acclaimed series to test her wiles in a new and disturbing manner. When a murdered author is found in her home, investigators are left with little to know insight, which bothers Scarpetta almost as much as the slaying itself. Questions grow exponentially while answers remain deftly hidden behind layers of the victim’s past. Scarpetta and the police being piecing things together, discovering a deeper back story related to her current piece of work and a collection of letters she wrote to a mysterious ‘M’. After a related murder, Scarpetta realises there is more to the story than meets the eye. When an old flame resurfaces, he could be the key to putting it all together or the impediment that the killer needs to make a clean getaway. As things begin to come together on one level, they unravel before Scarpetta can make sense of all the gathered evidence. Will the killer slide back into obscurity before being called out to face justice? A brilliant, thought-provoking novel that will lead fans of the genre begging for more. Great character back story strengthens the foundation of both the novel and the series, still in its infancy.<br /><br />Cornwell does a fabulous job with all aspects of the novel. I must keep reminding myself that she forged the way in the genre, where characters such as Tempe Brennan and Megan Hunt followed suit with their own medical sleuthing. Scarpetta does defy the modern female protagonist with her crass perspective and vices galore. A great series for Reichs’ fans to try, while waiting for the next novel. Sure not to disappoint the reader who keeps an open mind. Any fan loving a great murder mystery with a hands-on medical professional will surely eat this up.<br /><br />Kudos, Madam Cornwell. I am a fan and cannot get enough of these books.<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_210816014">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/210816014" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5578999-charlynn" class="left imgcol" title="Charlynn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1307372670p2/5578999.jpg" alt="Charlynn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/210816014?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 25, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5578999-charlynn" class="user" title="Charlynn">Charlynn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/132336.Body_of_Evidence" title="Paperback 9780743493918" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer210816014">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16473591998825947804">A good murder mystery needs three key components: a sympathetic victim, a fast pace, and an intricately woven web of clues for the reader to unravel right along with the book's crime solving entities. Cornwell's Body of Evidence meets these standards. Right out of the gate, she introduces the victim, Beryl Madison, through the woman's own words – sharing with readers letters written by Beryl to the mysterious 'M,' a moniker later revealed to be a red herring. As more characters are introduced, t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16473591998825947804">A good murder mystery needs three key components: a sympathetic victim, a fast pace, and an intricately woven web of clues for the reader to unravel right along with the book's crime solving entities. Cornwell's Body of Evidence meets these standards. Right out of the gate, she introduces the victim, Beryl Madison, through the woman's own words – sharing with readers letters written by Beryl to the mysterious 'M,' a moniker later revealed to be a red herring. As more characters are introduced, the plot thickens, for it becomes quickly apparent that, concerning this case, no one is telling the truth. What is perhaps Body of Evidence's best asset, though, is the fact that despite Kay Scarpetta – Virginia's chief medical examiner and the novel's narrator's – intelligence and scientific training, its her intuitiveness and her heart which eventually help her to solve Beryl's murder. Just as readers come to care for the victim, so does Kay, and she resolves the mystery in a fashion that the audience can identify with. Although a crime novel told from a medical examiner's perspective could quickly become detached emotionally, there's nothing cold and sterile about Scarpetta's methods, this book, or Cornwell's abilities as an author.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16473591998825947804">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_781309797">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/781309797" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2224950-kathryn" class="left imgcol" title="Kathryn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1428875161p2/2224950.jpg" alt="Kathryn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/781309797?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 11, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2224950-kathryn" class="user" title="Kathryn">Kathryn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6817369-body-of-evidence" title="Hardcover 0684192405" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2224950-kathryn?shelf=2013" class="actionLinkLite">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer781309797">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7059346213029947166">This is the second Kay Scarpetta murder mystery, and I found it even better than the first one, if only because the killer did not come out of nothing, but was previously mentioned in passing earlier in the book. (Scarpetta observes in this book that murder does not happen in a vacuum; everything is connected somehow. And that is also how murder mystery novels should be.)<br /><br />It is 1987, a year after the previous book; Kay Scarpetta is still the Chief Medical Examiner for Virginia, Pete Marino is now</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7059346213029947166">This is the second Kay Scarpetta murder mystery, and I found it even better than the first one, if only because the killer did not come out of nothing, but was previously mentioned in passing earlier in the book. (Scarpetta observes in this book that murder does not happen in a vacuum; everything is connected somehow. And that is also how murder mystery novels should be.)<br /><br />It is 1987, a year after the previous book; Kay Scarpetta is still the Chief Medical Examiner for Virginia, Pete Marino is now a Lieutenant Detective (giving him even more freedom to be Scarpetta’s personal go-to policeman), and Benton Wesley is still an FBI Profiler. Scarpetta makes the post-mortem acquaintance of Beryl Madison, a minor novelist who has written her books under various pen names rather than under her real name. Madison is also the protégé of Cary Harper, who wrote one novel twenty years before that won the Pulitzer Prize, and who has lived an extraordinarily reclusive life since, refusing to give interviews and not writing. Madison apparently lived with Harper and his sister for many years; and there are rumors that the book she was working on was autobiographical, which would cause a sensation in the writing world.<br /><br />However, Madison was also being stalked; she fled to Key West, then returned to Richmond some months later, promptly being brutally murdered in her house mere hours after her return. No novel was found, only two photo-copied letters she had written while in Key West to someone named “M.” In the course of her investigation Scarpetta makes the re-acquaintance of an old flame, one whom she loved to distraction much more than he loved her, and finds herself being sued by an entertainment lawyer for having “stolen” the novel Madison had been writing. Things get even more complicated, and Scarpetta finds herself being stalked, apparently by Madison’s killer.<br /><br />This was a very good book, and I very much enjoyed reading it; but I will give Scarpetta a rest, and read one of the hundreds of books I own that I have not read yet before I return to her.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7059346213029947166">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/39460694?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 06, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1711431-eric-w" class="user" title="Eric_W">Eric_W</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/132336.Body_of_Evidence" title="Paperback 9780743493918" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1711431-eric-w?shelf=mysteries-and-thrillers" class="actionLinkLite">mysteries-and-thrillers</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39460694">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8602816535295673047">The heroine is Dr. Kay Scarpetta, the Chief Medical Examiner in Virginia. Oh, no, you say, another Ouincv. Wrong, corpse-breath. Scarpetta is intelligent, short, (we don't know whether she is attractive or not, a relief) and she doesn't swoon over each drooling Sylvester Stallone imitation that happens by. (That's something I've always wondered about: How does Travis McGee, the blue-Rolls-Royce-truck-driving hero of John MacDonald's colored-titled novels avoid AIDS, since he seems to have the se</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8602816535295673047">The heroine is Dr. Kay Scarpetta, the Chief Medical Examiner in Virginia. Oh, no, you say, another Ouincv. Wrong, corpse-breath. Scarpetta is intelligent, short, (we don't know whether she is attractive or not, a relief) and she doesn't swoon over each drooling Sylvester Stallone imitation that happens by. (That's something I've always wondered about: How does Travis McGee, the blue-Rolls-Royce-truck-driving hero of John MacDonald's colored-titled novels avoid AIDS, since he seems to have the self-restraint of a male nymphomaniac?<br /> Anyway, Scarpetta is investigating the murder of a well-known novelist who has returned from the Florida Keys where she has been hiding from someone who keeps threatening to kill her. The night of her return she inexplicably opens the door to the murderer who does just that. The plot thickens as her former boyfriend, a lawyer, appears on the scene worried about her safety and to prevent her (he says) from crossing swords with a crooked entertainment lawyer (redundancy?) who desperately wants the victim's last manuscript. The book is filled with fascinating detail such as the difference between dextromethorphan and levomethorpan which has to do with right and left and why one is legal and the other not. Enough about the plot. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_278357998">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/278357998" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1353392-emily" class="left imgcol" title="Emily"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1298937060p2/1353392.jpg" alt="Emily" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/278357998?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 15, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1353392-emily" class="user" title="Emily">Emily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/132336.Body_of_Evidence" title="Paperback 9780743493918" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer278357998">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13510348375548586122">An author receiving threatening phone calls decides to hide for a while down in Key West and work on her memoir. She’s murdered the very night she sets foot back in Richmond. Kay Scarpetta, Richmond Chief Medical Examiner, investigates the case along with the intensely dislikable Lieutenant Marino. It looks like a psycho stalker did the deed, but the missing manuscript has an unscrupulous and greedy agent complicating the investigation in order to get his hands on the valuable pages.<br /><br /><br /><br />Cornwell’s w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13510348375548586122">An author receiving threatening phone calls decides to hide for a while down in Key West and work on her memoir. She’s murdered the very night she sets foot back in Richmond. Kay Scarpetta, Richmond Chief Medical Examiner, investigates the case along with the intensely dislikable Lieutenant Marino. It looks like a psycho stalker did the deed, but the missing manuscript has an unscrupulous and greedy agent complicating the investigation in order to get his hands on the valuable pages.<br /><br /><br /><br />Cornwell’s writing is fast paced, technical enough to be realistic to those familiar with law enforcement and psychiatry, but also understandable to the lay person (although I’m not sure why the ME is getting so involved, it’s been my experience that they mostly limit their investigations to autopsies and evidence found on the body).<br /><br />Unlike a lot of female protagonists in crime novels, I can’t fault Kay very much with putting herself in dangerous situations, but again, she does get much more involved with the case than one would expect from someone in her job description and much, much closer to the killer than necessary.<br /><br /><br /><br />I mentioned this in my review of the first Kay Scarpetta book, <em>Postmortem</em> but it bears repeating: if your lengthy and intensive investigation leads you almost to the point where you know who/where your killer is and said killer shows up at the protagonist’s home/work/favorite restaurant, etc. and tries to kill him or her, your entire investigation is pointless. You pretty much could have waited until he showed up and saved yourself a lot of trouble. I get that it’s nice to have a suspenseful, dangerous climax, but that does not have to happen on the investigator’s own turf.<br /><br /><br /><br />I like a good crime novel, and this had enough twists, turns, and possible suspects to keep me entertained, but the ending seemed a little pat and coincidental. I would rate it as average. 3 stars.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13510348375548586122">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer166029142">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10092989393066501705">Why read: Reading the series.<br /><br />What impressed me: Body of Evidence was definitely a topsy-turvy mystery. Not only do you not know what's going on with the victims, you really don't have nay clue who to trust in the investigation either. Kay's not knowing friend from foe in her personal life adds a lot of tension and intrigue to the story. And either Cornwell does much better in this second book with laying off the excessive explanations, or I'm just getting used to her writing style.<br /><br />What disappoin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10092989393066501705">Why read: Reading the series.<br /><br />What impressed me: Body of Evidence was definitely a topsy-turvy mystery. Not only do you not know what's going on with the victims, you really don't have nay clue who to trust in the investigation either. Kay's not knowing friend from foe in her personal life adds a lot of tension and intrigue to the story. And either Cornwell does much better in this second book with laying off the excessive explanations, or I'm just getting used to her writing style.<br /><br />What disappointed me: Nothing stood out as disappointing. Well, except the crazed homophobia of law enforcement. Was it really that extreme in the early 90s when this book first came out?<br /><br />Recommended: Yes. Even better than the last.<br /><br />Continue series: Yes. I'm definitely becoming interested in Kay's personal life.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_271253151">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271253151" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2763719-john" class="left imgcol" title="John"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1386501977p2/2763719.jpg" alt="John" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/271253151?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 04, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2763719-john" class="user" title="John">John</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=mystery-detective-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-detective-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer271253151">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16543682966279780012">A solid murder mystery that, thankfully, does not rely too much on the forensic science element to further the plot. Cornwell is a terrific writer, and I enjoy her Kay Scarpetta character more than most detectives from other series. The book is fun and light, never disappointing but never reaching the upper echelons of great storytelling, either. Great for a long airplane ride, but not a book you're likely to remember well a couple years after you read it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/3944911-nimue" class="user" title="Nimue">Nimue</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer401271495">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13238952843348887033">I read Patricia cornwell's novel " Book of the dead " two years back and I still can remember the craze it became for me that weekend to finish it and reach the end. After months ( probably the 2nd or 3rd time this year ) , i felt the same obsession in me.<br /><br />The book follows the life of a writer Beryl who for some reasons writes under different names for each of her book and was on a run days before she is killed in her own home. The book engages you from the beginning with the letters she writes t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13238952843348887033">I read Patricia cornwell's novel " Book of the dead " two years back and I still can remember the craze it became for me that weekend to finish it and reach the end. After months ( probably the 2nd or 3rd time this year ) , i felt the same obsession in me.<br /><br />The book follows the life of a writer Beryl who for some reasons writes under different names for each of her book and was on a run days before she is killed in her own home. The book engages you from the beginning with the letters she writes to a certain "M" ; with the stated fact that she opened the door to the killer even when she was scared enough to hide from the world till then. Then there is the odd mentor who is first thought as the man behind her killing and later the victim too.The simple looking plot goes on to link different people in unimaginable ways to the story - Beryl's friends , friend's friends, police , cheif medical officer , patient of a mental hospital , lawyers of entertainment industry and so on. Every answer is another question towards solving the mystery but question still. Its not till the end that the puzzle starts solving itself in your head and yet you have to read to make sense of few things that still are hazy in your understanding. The medical officer Scarpetta is intutive , sensitive, focussed and as humane as you can imagine. Married to her work , and living with a not so happy past , she is not the super hero you simply admire. she is the character you want to be inspired from. Patricia knows her art really well. I am totally into reading her other books soon</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13238952843348887033">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_341748246">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/341748246" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5422636-c-c-thomas" class="left imgcol" title="C.C. Thomas"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1390405747p2/5422636.jpg" alt="C.C. Thomas" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/341748246?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 04, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5422636-c-c-thomas" class="user" title="C.C. Thomas">C.C. Thomas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/132336.Body_of_Evidence" title="Paperback 9780743493918" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5422636-c-c-thomas?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer341748246">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6093956346445388712">This was so so different from the first one! I expected the same basic plot, as is the case with most mystery series, and I would have been fine with that because I loved the first one. But Cornwell really threw me for a surprise in this second installment. For a woman (Kay Scarpetta) who is so obviously a control freak, she is really pushing her own comfort boundary to solve this case as a DE of Virginia. <br /><br />Scarpetta is called in to investigate the death of a young novelist. As she begins on what</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6093956346445388712">This was so so different from the first one! I expected the same basic plot, as is the case with most mystery series, and I would have been fine with that because I loved the first one. But Cornwell really threw me for a surprise in this second installment. For a woman (Kay Scarpetta) who is so obviously a control freak, she is really pushing her own comfort boundary to solve this case as a DE of Virginia. <br /><br />Scarpetta is called in to investigate the death of a young novelist. As she begins on what seems to be a clear cut case, she is soon trapped in a sticky web of deceit that involves abuse, love triangles, secret manuscripts and a family secret that is murky and tragic. Scarpetta leaves Virgina to chase down the truth and I like the break in the routine. The ending and plot twists are full of surprises the whole way through and I didn't know what to expect from one chapter to another.<br /><br />I can tell this isn't going to be a regular murder mystery series but a series about a complex woman using her brain to solve a murder. Unique! I have a feeling Scarpetta and I are going to become great friends. I can't wait to read the next one and get to know her better. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6093956346445388712">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer49327882">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13231202353124432699">A major problem for Ms Cornwell is often to figure out how the perpetrator does things, for example, gaining access to premises where the potential victims are already on their guard. This problem is solved very cleverly in this book, and the narrative and forensics are as well thought out as usual.<br /><br />For all that, it is not so involving as the first book in the Scarpetta series. For me the reason lies in the relationships between the characters being less intense and also less credible. I felt thi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13231202353124432699">A major problem for Ms Cornwell is often to figure out how the perpetrator does things, for example, gaining access to premises where the potential victims are already on their guard. This problem is solved very cleverly in this book, and the narrative and forensics are as well thought out as usual.<br /><br />For all that, it is not so involving as the first book in the Scarpetta series. For me the reason lies in the relationships between the characters being less intense and also less credible. I felt this particularly with the 'love interest', which I did not believe. An old flame being rekindled is always possible, but quite a time had passed. And then there is the apparently dubious behaviour of the man in question who, in the end, turns out to have been on the side of the angels after all, working undercover for the FBI. (Or was it the CIA?)<br />This had a slightly clichéd feel to me. <br /><br />By her own high standards this is very competent but it is not one of her best books.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer272765648">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8143909687863270310">Cornwell's stories are interesting. She obviously knows her forensics and related protocols. Her character, Kay Scarpetta is the holier than though, smarter than though, success in the family - and yet her focus is on her lacking areas. She's a renowned doctor and an attorney - yet she invariably finds her position in jeopardy because of the perfect work she does. Some of her books are wonderful - and some go too far with the ghoulish details. Kay is likable - but sometimes her superiority is of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8143909687863270310">Cornwell's stories are interesting. She obviously knows her forensics and related protocols. Her character, Kay Scarpetta is the holier than though, smarter than though, success in the family - and yet her focus is on her lacking areas. She's a renowned doctor and an attorney - yet she invariably finds her position in jeopardy because of the perfect work she does. Some of her books are wonderful - and some go too far with the ghoulish details. Kay is likable - but sometimes her superiority is offensive. Comparing her to a down-to-earth detective who is madly in love with her but never good enough because he isn't blindingly handsome, highly educated and acclaimed in a sophisticated field (ie. he's not a world-famous profiler for the FBI) comes across as a form of discrimination. <br /><br />Her writing is very good, her story line is engaging - if she could just get rid of some of the gratuitous nonsense - she'd be perfect. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14393991939516645587">As good as the first novel, but with a twist that at times almost had me lost! Think this could have been a very confusing read had I not been continuously reading - definitely not a book to read slowly. That being said, the drama built up around Kay Scarpetta in this novel did make for a much more compulsive read than the first, meaning that it was difficult to put down. I think I preferred this story more than the first. <br /><br />I was a bit disappointed to find that a lot of the characters mentioned i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14393991939516645587">As good as the first novel, but with a twist that at times almost had me lost! Think this could have been a very confusing read had I not been continuously reading - definitely not a book to read slowly. That being said, the drama built up around Kay Scarpetta in this novel did make for a much more compulsive read than the first, meaning that it was difficult to put down. I think I preferred this story more than the first. <br /><br />I was a bit disappointed to find that a lot of the characters mentioned in the first book were not mentioned in this book, and the introduction of a lot of new characters made it difficult for me to keep track of who was who. Still, an enjoyable read, and am looking forward to reading the next Scarpetta novel!</span>

The core of the emerging Scarpetta series is Dr. Scarpetta-forensic pathologist, Pete Marino-Detective, Benton Wesley-Profiler, Lucy-Scarpetta's niece. The main victim in this book is a writer. There's a romantic relationship for Scarpetta, some interesting references to same sex relationships as if Cornwell is laying the foundation for something to come. I enjoyed the story and in her usual fashion the killer is revealed near the end. Dr. Scarpetta is a woman who enjoys her cigarettes and high-priced booze perhaps to overcome her stressful job.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1493994520">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9483713157344157792">Reading crime thrillers is one of my guilty pleasures. Suffice to say I like this series more than a bit - now that I have finished this book just a day after I finished Post Mortem. This book deals with the murder of a writer who has been traumatized for months by a caller threatening and antagonizing her. Without going into specifics, let me say that the story line is slick and the plot keeps you hooked till the end with its twists and turns. The relationship between Scarpetta and Marino is al</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9483713157344157792">Reading crime thrillers is one of my guilty pleasures. Suffice to say I like this series more than a bit - now that I have finished this book just a day after I finished Post Mortem. This book deals with the murder of a writer who has been traumatized for months by a caller threatening and antagonizing her. Without going into specifics, let me say that the story line is slick and the plot keeps you hooked till the end with its twists and turns. The relationship between Scarpetta and Marino is also fleshed out and a chemistry seems to be blossoming between them in this one. What I don't like is how a sensible person like Scarpetta gets entangled and always become the target of people who she is supposed to help the police convict in the first place. The unnecessary romance angle between Mark and Scarpetta in the end also seems out of place. Again, since the setting is 90s some of the police procedures and forensic techniques seem rudimentary. But as far as the genre goes, this series seems very promising.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9483713157344157792">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5598612-andreia-silva?shelf=biblioteca" class="actionLinkLite">biblioteca</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5598612-andreia-silva?shelf=desafio-livros-biblioteca-2014-bdl" class="actionLinkLite">desafio-livros-biblioteca-2014-bdl</a>,

              <a href="/review/list/5598612-andreia-silva?shelf=desafio-alfabeto-2014-ewdigb" class="actionLinkLite">desafio-alfabeto-2014-ewdigb</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer859603538">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8827717993393015296">Depois da leitura deste segundo volume da série policial com a médica legista Kay Scarpetta, já assimilei a fórmula Cornwell. Pode ser por este ser apenas o segundo volume, mas não me parece que a autora irá fugir do seu estilo de policial nos próximos enredos, mas cá estarei para o confirmar.<br /><br />Patricia Cornwell, em "Corpo de Delito", mostra-nos que os crimes, a maioria das vezes estão ligados entre teias intrincadas de vários acontecimentos em efeito dominó. Tudo começa com o assassínio de uma es</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8827717993393015296">Depois da leitura deste segundo volume da série policial com a médica legista Kay Scarpetta, já assimilei a fórmula Cornwell. Pode ser por este ser apenas o segundo volume, mas não me parece que a autora irá fugir do seu estilo de policial nos próximos enredos, mas cá estarei para o confirmar.<br /><br />Patricia Cornwell, em "Corpo de Delito", mostra-nos que os crimes, a maioria das vezes estão ligados entre teias intrincadas de vários acontecimentos em efeito dominó. Tudo começa com o assassínio de uma escritora apavorada por andar a ser perseguida, morrendo quando abre a porta ao seu assassino.<br /><br />O facto de haver uma fórmula não significa que o livro é mau ou que é previsível do tipo sei-logo-quem-é-o-assassino mas, porque, mais uma vez, o crime se envolve na vida da médica legista e se envolve no passado de Scarpetta. A investigação que ela faz nunca é totalmente imparcial e nunca é fria o suficiente para o ser. Chega, no entanto, a ser um ponto positivo, uma vez que nos mostra que ela é, para além de policial, um ser humano.<br /><br />Mas agradou-me todo o desenvolvimento da trama e o modo como a autora nos leva atrás de Scarpetta na busca do assassino. Toda a investigação policial e as técnicas forenses, bem patentes no livro, despertam a curiosidade no leitor e incentivam a virar a página. Quem venham os próximos!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_840935474">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/840935474" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6848701-timothy-darling" class="left imgcol" title="Timothy Darling"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1360177299p2/6848701.jpg" alt="Timothy Darling" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/840935474?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 01, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6848701-timothy-darling" class="user" title="Timothy Darling">Timothy Darling</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/484957.Body_of_Evidence" title="Audio CD 9780788733970" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6848701-timothy-darling?shelf=period-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">period-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6848701-timothy-darling?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6848701-timothy-darling?shelf=suspense" class="actionLinkLite">suspense</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6848701-timothy-darling?shelf=travel" class="actionLinkLite">travel</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6848701-timothy-darling?shelf=psychology" class="actionLinkLite">psychology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer840935474">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6806534668959066050">My second time through this book I liked it better. It has been nearly five years since I read it so I was not completely expecting every twist, especially the one involving Mark, so it was like reading it for the first time again. Kay Scarpetta is, of course, the chief medical examiner for Virginia. As such she carries some weight, but seems a little weak as a character. I liked her relationship with Moreno but the DA and some of her office cohorts could have been more fully developed. I liked</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6806534668959066050">My second time through this book I liked it better. It has been nearly five years since I read it so I was not completely expecting every twist, especially the one involving Mark, so it was like reading it for the first time again. Kay Scarpetta is, of course, the chief medical examiner for Virginia. As such she carries some weight, but seems a little weak as a character. I liked her relationship with Moreno but the DA and some of her office cohorts could have been more fully developed. I liked the victims. This might be one of the best strengths of the book. Cornwell developed her victims more fully than some of her living characters, so Beryl Madison especially had a strong presence. Unfortunately some of the fullness of her character was hampered by the need for suspense in the book. Her character unfolding was too slow, so she could not fill out as much as she might have. However, I could sincerely wish to be able to read some of the tragic writers books, especially the lost manuscript.<br /><br />Last time I read this book I noted the gay fear and the smoking and their relationship to the setting of the book. This time through, I had recently been looking at another book in which the two ideas are highlighted from the perspective of the 1960s. The attitudes about both social issues have radically changed in the last 50 years and these two writers capture the transition well. Both Cornwell and King attempt to engage equal repulsion for smoking and homophobia. It is not effective for me, but I do find the observation of the difference interesting.<br /><br />Read Cornwell for a well developed protagonist. Scarpetta is vulnerable and determined. With the cookie cutter forensic shows on TV, I found myself wondering why some of the discoveries that needed to be made took so long, but then I remembered this was the 80s, not the 21st century.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6806534668959066050">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_190297767">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190297767" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1876057-emily-c" class="left imgcol" title="emily c."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1295925950p2/1876057.jpg" alt="emily c." /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/190297767?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 27, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1876057-emily-c" class="user" title="emily c.">emily c.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/132336.Body_of_Evidence" title="Paperback 9780743493918" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1876057-emily-c?shelf=patricia-cornwell" class="actionLinkLite">patricia-cornwell</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer190297767">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6327343490773684494">I think it is not as good as other Scarpetta novels. The plot is somewhat loose and compressed only at the end. There is not much thrill reading this one, less gore, too much drama and quite uninteresting characters, especially the killer. A schizophrenic killer, with childhood troubles is frankly common. Though most murderers are loose in the head, writers of this genre must make the person interesting and amuse the readers on the workings of a criminally insane mind as Cornwell has done in her</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6327343490773684494">I think it is not as good as other Scarpetta novels. The plot is somewhat loose and compressed only at the end. There is not much thrill reading this one, less gore, too much drama and quite uninteresting characters, especially the killer. A schizophrenic killer, with childhood troubles is frankly common. Though most murderers are loose in the head, writers of this genre must make the person interesting and amuse the readers on the workings of a criminally insane mind as Cornwell has done in her other books; in this one her characterization of the killer fell flat.<br /><br />One thing I am starting to feel as a reader of this series (though I did not read the books in order) is that the focus on Kay Scarpetta has become somewhat tiring. Somehow she ends up always at the center of everything that happens, even the killings turn out to involve her personally; it is always about her. It may be understandable as she is, after all, the hero, the protagonist of this series, but it maybe good to give her a break and make the character see that not everything is about her. A little less focus on the hero perhaps and more on the killers, victims and the amazing technical details will probably help refresh the readers of the wonderful complexity and excitement expected from books in this genre.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6327343490773684494">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IZtN0LGA0LKPCGUH80Xd560ZTRnKvlpcetNvTGdJp+FET3IDQ1LESAPQEbyNJDtV5O6OAINjHfYQ2mreq9xRpA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

Fatal Cure is a hair-raising, timely foray into the dark side of medical reform, proving that with &amp;quot;managed care&amp;quot; the unthinkable can be as close as the local hospital. Doctors Angela and David Wilson believe they have found personal and professional bliss when they opt to leave the university medical center for Bartlet Community Hospital, a modern, state-of-the-art medical facility in scenic Bartlet, Vermont. For Angela, a pathologist, and David, an internist/primary-care physician, Bartlet seems to be a dream come true: a town with green lawns and crystal lakes that is an idyllic haven from urban crime and pollution; a chance for a home of their own and a resurgence of romance in their relationship; a perfect environment for their eight-year-old daughter, Nikki, who suffers from cystic fibrosis; and the opportunity to work within an enlightened system of &amp;quot;managed care.&amp;quot; But all is not what it seems. After a resplendent fall, a stark landscape looms in Bartlet that reveals more than the skeletons of the trees. Gradually at first and then at a quickening pace, the Wilsons\' earthly Nirvana disintegrates as mysterious, unexplained deaths become more than coincidences. The deadly nightmare of their life threatens them all, even Nikki, the most vulnerable. Fighting for their careers as well as for the very survival of their family, Angela and David must conquer the evil that confronts each of them before they are consumed by the horror.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1025097.Patricia_Cornwell">About Patricia Cornwell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1025097.Patricia_Cornwell"><img alt="1025097" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1442522626p2/1025097.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer7179093128909786096">Patricia Cornwell sold her first novel, Postmortem, in 1990 while working as a computer analyst at the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner in Richmond, Virginia. Postmortem, was the first bona fide forensic thriller. It paved the way for an explosion of entertainment featuring in all things forensic across film, television and literature. <br /><br />Postmortem would go on to win the Edgar, Creasey, Anthony,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7179093128909786096">Patricia Cornwell sold her first novel, Postmortem, in 1990 while working as a computer analyst at the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner in Richmond, Virginia. Postmortem, was the first bona fide forensic thriller. It paved the way for an explosion of entertainment featuring in all things forensic across film, television and literature. <br /><br />Postmortem would go on to win the Edgar, Creasey, Anthony, and Macavity awards as well as the French Prix du Roman d’Aventure prize – the first book ever to claim all these distinctions in a single year. To date, Cornwell’s books have sold some 100 million copies in thirty-six languages in over 120 countries. She’s authored twenty-nine New York Times bestsellers.<br /><br />Patricia’s novels center primarily on medical examiner Kay Scarpetta along with her tech-savvy niece Lucy and fellow investigator Pete Marino. Celebrating 25 years, these characters have grown into an international phenomenon, winning Cornwell the Sherlock Award for best detective created by an American author, the Gold Dagger Award, the RBA Thriller Award, and the Medal of Chevalier of the Order of Arts and Letters for her contributions to literary and artistic development. <br /><br />Fox 2000 bought the rights to Kay Scarpetta. Working with producer Liz Friedman, Marvel’s Jessica Jones and fellow Marvel EP and Twilight Saga scribe Melissa Rosenberg to develop the film and find Scarpetta a home on the big screen. <br /><br />After earning her degree in English from Davidson College in 1979, she began working at the Charlotte Observer. <br /><br />Cornwell received widespread attention and praise for her series of articles on prostitution and crime in downtown Charlotte. From the Charlotte Observer, Cornwell moved to a job with the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner of Virginia – a post she would later bestow upon the fictional Kay Scarpetta. <br /><br />When not writing from her Boston home, Patricia tirelessly researches cutting-edge forensic technologies to include in her work. Her interests span outside the literary: Patricia co-founded of the Conservation Scientist Chair at the Harvard University Art Museums. She appears as a forensic consultant on CNN and serves as a member of Harvard-affiliated McLean Hospital’s National Council, where she advocates for psychiatric research. She’s helped fund the ICU at Cornell’s Animal Hospital, the scientific study of a Confederate submarine, the archaeological excavation of Jamestown, and a variety of law enforcement charities. Patricia is also committed to <br />funding scholarships and literacy programs. Her advice to aspiring authors: “Start writing. And don’t take no for an answer.” <br /><br /><br />Social and Digital Outlets<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.patriciacornwell.com" target="_blank">http://www.patriciacornwell.com</a> <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/patricia.cornwell" target="_blank">https://www.facebook.com/patricia.cor...</a> <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/1pcornwell" target="_blank">https://twitter.com/1pcornwell</a> <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="https://instagram.com/1pcornwell/" target="_blank">https://instagram.com/1pcornwell/</a><br /><br /><br />Other areas of expertise &amp; interests<br />Forensics | Forensic Technologies | Ballistics | Weapons | Explosives | Pathology &amp; Autopsies | Crime | Historical and Unsolved Criminal Cases | Jack The Ripper | Helicopter Piloting | Suba Diving | Archaeological Excavation Experience |</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7179093128909786096">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/1025097.Patricia_Cornwell" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Patricia Cornwell...</a>

That\'s w&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText4483356496303353713\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;See alternate cover edition here\n\nVirginia Medical Examiner Kay Scarpetta has a bloody puzzle on her hands: five headless, limbless cadavers in Ireland, plus four similar victims in a landfill back home. Is a serial butcher loose in Virginia? That\'s what the panicked public thinks, thanks to a local TV reporter who got the leaked news from her boyfriend, Scarpetta\'s vile rival, Investigator Percy Ring. But the butchered bodies are so many red herrings intended to throw idiots like Ring off the track. Instead of a run-of-the-mill serial killer, we\'re dealing with a shadowy figure who has plans involving mutant smallpox, mass murder, and messing with Scarpetta\'s mind by e-mailing her gory photos of the murder scenes, along with cryptic AOL chat-room messages. The coolest innovation: Scarpetta\'s gorgeous genius niece, Lucy, equips her with a DataGlove and a VPL Eyephone, and she takes a creepy virtual tour of the e-mailed crime scene.\n\nUnnatural Exposure boasts brisk storytelling, crackling dialogue, evocative prose about forensic-science sleuthing, and crisp character sketches, both of familiar characters like Scarpetta\'s gruff partner Pete Marino and bit players like the landfill employee falsely accused by Ring. Plus, let\'s face it: serial killers are old hat. Cornwell\'s most vivid villains are highly plausible backstabbing colleagues like Ring, who plots to destroy Lucy\'s FBI career by outing her as a lesbian. Some readers object to the rather abrupt ending, but, hey, it\'s less jarring than Hannibal\'s, and it\'s the logical culmination of Cornwell\'s philosophy about human nature.       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2361096-body-of-evidence">Quotes from Body of Evidence</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Has all the trappings of a mystery novel, doesn't it?”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/398599-has-all-the-trappings-of-a-mystery-novel-doesn-t-it" class="actionLinkLite">10 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“I didn't know what I wanted. Maybe I never had. The emotional distance was never worth the togetherness, and yet I didn't learn. Nothing had changed. Had he reached for me, I would have forgotten to behave sensibly. Desire has no reason, and the need for intimacy had never stopped. I had not conjured up the images in years, his lips on mine, his hands, the urgency of our hunger. Now I was tormented by the memories.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/914905-i-didn-t-know-what-i-wanted-maybe-i-never-had" class="actionLinkLite">3 likes</a>
